{"content_type": "text/x-markdown", "avatar_url": "https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/facce030b679bda34eb7c64885a741fc?d=identicon", "timestamp": 1375824454, "display_recipient": "programming", "sender_id": 2110, "sender_full_name": "Eric Weinstein", "sender_domain": "students.hackerschool.com", "content": "Got it. I'm not overly familiar with Python/CodeIgniter, but my take would be to:\n1. Sketch out some of the basics, e.g. what models you think you'll need;\n2. Write some tests for those models (e.g. a test to ensure that your User model has an e-mail attribute)\n3. Run your tests, watch them fail\n4. Write the code that makes your tests NOT fail\n\nI hope this doesn't sound way too simplistic; it's a deceptively simple model that makes tons of sense when you get it, but no sense at all when you haven't done it before", "gravatar_hash": "facce030b679bda34eb7c64885a741fc", "recipient_id": 20203, "client": "website", "sender_email": "eric.q.weinstein@gmail.com", "subject_links": [], "subject": "testing", "type": "stream", "id": 8822973, "sender_short_name": "eric.q.weinstein"}

The idea is to synthesize a program that manipulates bit vectors by providing input-output examples. For example, say you want to turn off the right-most contiguous string of on bits: `[1 0 1 1 0] => [1 0 0 0 0]`. A naive O(n) solution is obvious, but a fast and tricky solution might not be.
